<p>Further, if  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msub><mi mathvariant="normal">R</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">f</mi></msub><mo>=</mo><msub><mi mathvariant="normal">R</mi><mn>1</mn></msub></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\mathrm{R_f} = \mathrm{R_1}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8333em; vertical-align: -0.15em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm">R</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.3361em;"><span style="top: -2.55em; margin-left: 0em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mathrm mtight" style="margin-right: 0.07778em;">f</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8333em; vertical-align: -0.15em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm">R</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.3011em;"><span style="top: -2.55em; margin-left: 0em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mathrm mtight">1</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> , then</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msub><mi>V</mi><mn>0</mn></msub><mo>=</mo><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><msub><mi>V</mi><mn>2</mn></msub><mo>−</mo><msub><mi>V</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo stretchy="false">)</mo><mo>=</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">V_{0} = (V_{2} - V_{1}) =</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8333em; vertical-align: -0.15em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.22222em;">V</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.3011em;"><span style="top: -2.55em; margin-left: -0.2222em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight">0</span></span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1em; vertical-align: -0.25em;"></span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.22222em;">V</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.3011em;"><span style="top: -2.55em; margin-left: -0.2222em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight">2</span></span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">−</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1em; vertical-align: -0.25em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.22222em;">V</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.3011em;"><span style="top: -2.55em; margin-left: -0.2222em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight">1</span></span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mclose">)</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">=</span></span></span></span></span>  difference of the two input voltages and the circuit functions as a subtractor.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="6-7-6-integration-using-op-amp">6.7.6 Integration Using OP-AMP<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#6-7-6-integration-using-op-amp" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The function of an integrator is to provide an output voltage which is proportional to the integral of the input voltage.</p>
<p>Introduction to Operational Amplifiers</p>
<p>A simple example of integration is shown in Fig. 6.12(a), where input is dc voltage and its integral is a linearly-increasing ramp voltage.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-c71c6cab.jpeg" alt="img-13.jpeg">
Figure 6.12 (a) Input and output waveforms of an integrator circuit</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-ddaa48d6.jpeg" alt="img-14.jpeg"></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-23125005.jpeg" alt="img-15.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="circuit">Circuit<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#circuit" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The actual integrating circuit using OP-AMP is shown in Fig. 6.12 (b). The feedback component is a capacitor  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msub><mi>C</mi><mi>f</mi></msub></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">C_f</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.9694em; vertical-align: -0.2861em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.07153em;">C</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.3361em;"><span style="top: -2.55em; margin-left: -0.0715em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right: 0.10764em;">f</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.2861em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>  connected between input and output.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-cec495b3.jpeg" alt="img-16.jpeg">
Figure 6.12 (b) OP-AMP integrator circuit</p>
<p>As input current of OP-AMP is zero, the entire current I flowing through  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msub><mi mathvariant="bold">R</mi><mn>1</mn></msub></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\mathbf{R}_1</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8361em; vertical-align: -0.15em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathbf">R</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.3011em;"><span style="top: -2.55em; margin-left: 0em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight">1</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> , also flows through  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msub><mi mathvariant="bold">C</mi><mn>1</mn></msub></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\mathbf{C}_1</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8361em; vertical-align: -0.15em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathbf">C</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.3011em;"><span style="top: -2.55em; margin-left: 0em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight">1</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> ,</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="calculations">Calculations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#calculations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>From input side we can write</p>
<div class="math math-display"><span class="katex-display"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" display="block"><semantics><mtable width="100%"><mtr><mtd width="50%"></mtd><mtd><mrow><mi>I</mi><mo>=</mo><mfrac><mrow><msub><mi>V</mi><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">c</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">s</mi></mrow></msub><mo>−</mo><msub><mi>V</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">A</mi></msub></mrow><msub><mi>R</mi><mn>1</mn></msub></mfrac><mo>=</mo><mfrac><msub><mi>V</mi><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">c</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">s</mi></mrow></msub><msub><mi>R</mi><mn>1</mn></msub></mfrac></mrow></mtd><mtd width="50%"></mtd><mtd><mtext>(6.14)</mtext></mtd></mtr></mtable><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">I = \frac {V _ {\mathrm {c s}} - V _ {\mathrm {A}}}{R _ {1}} = \frac {V _ {\mathrm {c s}}}{R _ {1}} \tag {6.14}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.07847em;">I</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 2.1963em; <p>From output side we can write,</p>
<div class="math math-display"><span class="katex-display"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" display="block"><semantics><mrow><mi>I</mi><mo>=</mo><msub><mi>C</mi><mi>f</mi></msub><mfrac><mrow><mi>d</mi><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><msub><mi>V</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">A</mi></msub><mo>−</mo><msub><mi>V</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">c</mi></msub><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><mrow><mi>d</mi><mi>t</mi></mrow></mfrac></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">I = C _ {f} \frac {d (V _ {\mathrm {A}} - V _ {\mathrm {c}})}{d t}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.07847em;">I</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 2.113em; <p>Basic Electronics</p>

<p>Equating the two equations (6.14) and (6.15)</p>

<p>Integrating both sides,</p>

<div class="math math-display"><span class="katex-display"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" display="block"><semantics><mtable width="100%"><mtr><mtd width="50%"></mtd><mtd><mrow><msub><mi>V</mi><mi>n</mi></msub><mo>=</mo><mo>−</mo><mfrac><mn>1</mn><mrow><msub><mi>R</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><msub><mi>C</mi><mi>f</mi></msub></mrow></mfrac><msubsup><mo>∫</mo><mn>0</mn><mi>t</mi></msubsup><msub><mi>V</mi><mrow><mi>i</mi><mi>n</mi></mrow></msub><mi>d</mi><mi>t</mi><mo>+</mo><msub><mi>V</mi><mn>0</mn></msub><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mn>0</mn><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mtd><mtd width="50%"></mtd><mtd><mtext>(6.18)</mtext></mtd></mtr></mtable><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">V _ {n} = - \frac {1}{R _ {1} C _ {f}} \int_ {0} ^ {t} V _ {i n} d t + V _ {0} (0) \tag {6.18}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8333em; margin-left: -0.2222em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight">0</span></span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord">0</span><span class="mclose">)</span></span><span class="tag"><span class="strut" style="height: 2.5156em; vertical-align: -0.9721em;"></span><span class="mord text"><span class="mord">(</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord">6.18</span></span><span class="mord">)</span></span></span></span></span></span></div>
<p>where  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msub><mi mathvariant="normal">V</mi><mn>0</mn></msub><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mn>0</mn><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\mathrm{V}_0(0)</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1em; vertical-align: -0.25em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm" style="margin-right: 0.01389em;">V</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.3011em;"><span style="top: -2.55em; margin-left: -0.0139em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight">0</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord">0</span><span class="mclose">)</span></span></span></span></span>  is the constant of integration, indicating the initial output voltage. The equation (6.18) shows that the output is  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>−</mo><mn>1</mn><mi mathvariant="normal">/</mi><msub><mi mathvariant="normal">R</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><msub><mi mathvariant="normal">C</mi><mi>f</mi></msub></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">-1 / \mathrm{R}_1\mathrm{C}_f</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1.0361em; vertical-align: -0.2861em;"></span><span class="mord">−</span><span class="mord">1/</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm">R</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.3011em;"><span style="top: -2.55em; margin-left: 0em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight">1</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm">C</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.3361em;"><span style="top: -2.55em; margin-left: 0em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right: 0.10764em;">f</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.2861em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>  times the integral of input and  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msub><mi mathvariant="normal">R</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><msub><mi mathvariant="normal">C</mi><mi>f</mi></msub></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\mathrm{R}_1\mathrm{C}_f</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.9694em; vertical-align: -0.2861em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm">R</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.3011em;"><span style="top: -2.55em; margin-left: 0em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight">1</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm">C</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.3361em;"><span style="top: -2.55em; margin-left: 0em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right: 0.10764em;">f</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.2861em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>  is called time constant of the integrator.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="6-7-7-differentiation-using-op-amp">6.7.7 Differentiation using OP-AMP<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#6-7-7-differentiation-using-op-amp" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The function of a differentiator is to provide an output voltage which is proportional to the rate of change of the input voltage. It is an inverse mathematical operation to that of an integrator. As shown in Fig. 6.13, when we feed a ramp voltage to a differentiator, we get a constant dc voltage as output.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-458e007b.jpeg" alt="img-17.jpeg">
Figure 6.13 Input and output waveforms of a differentiator circuit</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-89a0d78d.jpeg" alt="img-18.jpeg"></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-16595aa3.jpeg" alt="img-19.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="circuit">Circuit<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#circuit" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Differentiator circuit can be obtained by interchanging the resistor and capacitor of integrator circuit as shown in Fig. 6.14. The node B is grounded. The node A is also at the virtual ground potential hence  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msub><mi>V</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">A</mi></msub><mo>=</mo><mn>0</mn></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">V_{\mathrm{A}} = 0</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8333em; vertical-align: -0.15em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.22222em;">V</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.3283em;"><span style="top: -2.55em; margin-left: -0.2222em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mathrm mtight">A</span></span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6444em;"></span><span class="mord">0</span></span></span></span></span> .</p>
<p>Introduction to Operational Amplifiers</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-743a6fde.jpeg" alt="img-20.jpeg">
Figure 6.14 OP-AMP differentiator</p>
<p>As input current of OP-AMP is zero, entire current  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msub><mi mathvariant="normal">I</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">t</mi></msub></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\mathrm{I}_{\mathrm{t}}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8333em; vertical-align: -0.15em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm">I</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.2806em;"><span style="top: -2.55em; margin-left: 0em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mathrm mtight">t</span></span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>  flows through the resistance  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msub><mi mathvariant="bold">R</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">r</mi></msub></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\mathbf{R}_{\mathrm{r}}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8361em; vertical-align: -0.15em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathbf">R</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.1514em;"><span style="top: -2.55em; margin-left: 0em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mathrm mtight">r</span></span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> .</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="calculations">Calculations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#calculations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>From the input side we can write,</p>
<div class="math math-display"><span class="katex-display"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" display="block"><semantics><mtable width="100%"><mtr><mtd width="50%"></mtd><mtd><mrow><msub><mi>I</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>=</mo><msub><mi>C</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mfrac><mrow><mi>d</mi><mrow><mo fence="true">(</mo><msub><mi>V</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">∞</mi></msub><mo>−</mo><msub><mi>V</mi><mi>A</mi></msub><mo fence="true">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mrow><mi>d</mi><mi>t</mi></mrow></mfrac><mo>=</mo><msub><mi>C</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mfrac><mrow><mi>d</mi><msub><mi>V</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">∞</mi></msub></mrow><mrow><mi>d</mi><mi>t</mi></mrow></mfrac></mrow></mtd><mtd width="50%"></mtd><mtd><mtext>(6.19)</mtext></mtd></mtr></mtable><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">I _ {1} = C _ {1} \frac {d \left(V _ {\infty} - V _ {A}\right)}{d t} = C _ {1} \frac {d V _ {\infty}}{d t} \tag {6.19}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8333em; vertical-align: -0.15em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.07847em;">I</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.3011em;"><span style="top: -2.55em; margin-left: -0.0785em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight">1</span></span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 2.113em; vertical-align: -0.686em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.07153em;">C</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.3011em;"><span style="top: -2.55em; <p>From the output side we can write,</p>

<p>Equating the two equations,</p>

margin-left: -0.0077em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right: 0.10764em;">f</span></span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.2861em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mord"><span class="mopen nulldelimiter"></span><span class="mfrac"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 1.3714em;"><span style="top: -2.314em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal">d</span><span class="mord mathnormal">t</span></span></span><span style="top: -3.23em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="frac-line" style="border-bottom-width: 0.04em;"></span></span><span style="top: -3.677em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal">d</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.22222em;">V</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.1514em;"><span style="top: -2.55em; margin-left: -0.2222em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight">∞</span></span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.686em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mclose nulldelimiter"></span></span></span><span class="tag"><span class="strut" style="height: 2.0574em; vertical-align: -0.686em;"></span><span class="mord text"><span class="mord">(</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord">6.22</span></span><span class="mord">)</span></span></span></span></span></span></div>
<p>The equation shows that the output is  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msub><mi>C</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><msub><mi>R</mi><mi>f</mi></msub></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">C_1R_f</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.9694em; vertical-align: -0.2861em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.07153em;">C</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.3011em;"><span style="top: -2.55em; margin-left: -0.0715em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight">1</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.00773em;">R</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.3361em;"><span style="top: -2.55em; margin-left: -0.0077em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right: 0.10764em;">f</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.2861em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>  times the differentiation of the input and product  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msub><mi>C</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><msub><mi>R</mi><mi>f</mi></msub></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">C_1R_f</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.9694em; vertical-align: -0.2861em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.07153em;">C</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.3011em;"><span style="top: -2.55em; margin-left: -0.0715em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight">1</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.00773em;">R</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.3361em;"><span style="top: -2.55em; margin-left: -0.0077em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right: 0.10764em;">f</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.2861em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>  is called time constant of the differentiator.</p>
<p>The negative sign indicates that there is a phase shift of  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msup><mn>180</mn><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">∘</mo></msup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">180^{\circ}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6741em;"></span><span class="mord">18</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord">0</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.6741em;"><span style="top: -3.063em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight">∘</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>  between input and output. The main advantage of such an active differentiator is the small time constant required for differentiation.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="6-8-cathode-ray-oscilloscope-cro">6.8 CATHODE RAY OSCILLOSCOPE (CRO)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#6-8-cathode-ray-oscilloscope-cro" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The Cathode Ray Oscilloscope (CRO) is an electronic device used to display and measure electrical quantities like a.c./d.c. voltages, time phase relationships, frequency, and a wide range of waveform characteristics like rise-time, fall-time, and overshoot etc. Non-electrical quantities like pressure, strain, temperature, and acceleration etc. can also be measured by converting them into an equivalent voltage and using different transducers.</p>
<p>Basic Electronics</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="6-8-1-block-diagram-of-cro">6.8.1 Block Diagram of CRO<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#6-8-1-block-diagram-of-cro" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-6e355899.jpeg" alt="img-21.jpeg">
Figure 6.15 Block diagram of CRO</p>
<p>The functions of various blocks of CRO (Fig. 6.15) are explained below:</p>
<ol>
<li>Cathode Ray Tube (CRT): This displays the quantity being measured.</li>
<li>Vertical Amplifier: It amplifies the signal waveform which is to be displayed.</li>
<li>Horizontal Amplifier: It is fed with a sawtooth voltage, which is then impressed upon the X-plates.</li>
<li>Sweep Generator: This produces a sawtooth voltage waveform, which is used for horizontal deflection of the electron beam.</li>
<li>Trigger Circuit: This generates trigger pulses to start horizontal sweep/scan.</li>
<li>High and Low-Voltage Power Supply.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="6-8-2-operation-of-a-cro">6.8.2 Operation of a CRO<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#6-8-2-operation-of-a-cro" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>A Cathode Ray Oscilloscope is a very useful and versatile laboratory instrument, used for measurement and analysis of waveforms and other phenomena of electronic circuits. It can allow viewing of signals of frequencies up to  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>50</mn><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">M</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">H</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">z</mi></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">50\mathrm{MHz}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord">50</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm">MHz</span></span></span></span></span></span>  or so and can provide number of waveform displays simultaneously on the screen. Two signals can be compared by applying them to separate channels. CRO has the ability to hold the displays of the signal on the screen for short or long time so that the original signal may be compared with the later applied signal.</p>
<p>For operation as an oscilloscope, the electron beam is deflected horizontally by a sweep voltage and vertically by the voltage to be measured. While the electron beam is moved across the screen of the CRT by the horizontal sweep signal, the input signal deflects the beam vertically, resulting in a display of the input signal waveform. One sweep of the beam scanned across the screen of the tube, followed by a "blank" period during which the beam is turned off while being returned to the starting point across the tube screen, constitutes one sweep of the beam. Steady display is obtained when the beam repeatedly sweeps across the tube with exactly the same image each sweep. This requires a synchronization, starting</p>
<p>Introduction to Operational Amplifiers</p>
<p>the sweep at the same point in a repetitive waveform cycle. If the signal is properly synchronized, the display will be stationary. In the absence of synchronization, the picture will appear to drift or move horizontally across the screen.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="6-8-3-cathode-ray-tube-crt">6.8.3 Cathode Ray Tube (CRT)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#6-8-3-cathode-ray-tube-crt" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>A cathode ray oscilloscope consists of a cathode ray tube (CRT), which is the heart of the oscilloscope, and some additional circuitry to operate the CRT (Fig. 6.16).</p>
<p>A CRT is an evacuated glass envelope of a special geometrical shape, which contains several electrodes. The cathode produces an electron beam, which is accelerated by the various electrodes into a high velocity beam called a cathode ray, which is then projected into the space of the tube, until it strikes the screen. A fluorescent material is coated to the internal portion of the screen to produce a spot of light, wherever electrons strike it. The electron beam may be deflected on its journey in any direction by appropriate magnetic or electrostatic fields.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-9e21e169.jpeg" alt="img-22.jpeg">
Figure 6.16 Cathode ray tube</p>
<p>The cathode ray tube consists of three sections:</p>
<p>(1) The electron gun, which produces, accelerates, and focuses the emitted electrons into a narrow beam.
(2) The deflection system, which deflects the electron beam either electrostatically or magnetically, in accordance with the current or voltage waveform to be displayed.
(3) A fluorescent screen, upon which the beam of electrons impinges, to produce a visible spot.</p>
<p>The Electron Gun: This consists of the Triode Section and the Focussing System.</p>
<p>(a) Triode Section: The grid, which is a nickel cup with a hole in it, almost completely encloses the cathode. The cathode, also made of nickel, is cylinder shaped, with a flat oxide-coated electron-emitting surface, directed towards the hole in the grid. Cathode is heated internally by a filament. The</p>
<p>Basic Electronics</p>
<p>cathode is at -2 KV, and the grid potential is adjustable from -2000 to -2050 Volts. Therefore, the grid potential controls the electron flow from the cathode, and this controls the number of electrons directed to the screen. A large number of electrons striking one point will cause the screen to glow brightly, and a small number of the same will produce a dim glow. Therefore, the grid potential controls the brightness (or intensity) on the screen.</p>
<p>The first anode, <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msub><mi>A</mi><mn>1</mn></msub></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">A_1</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8333em; vertical-align: -0.15em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal">A</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.3011em;"><span style="top: -2.55em; margin-left: 0em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight">1</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> is cylinder shaped, open at one end and closed at the other end, with a hole in its centre. Since <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msub><mi>A</mi><mn>1</mn></msub></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">A_1</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8333em; vertical-align: -0.15em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal">A</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.3011em;"><span style="top: -2.55em; margin-left: 0em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight">1</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> is grounded, and the cathode is at a high negative potential, <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msub><mi>A</mi><mn>1</mn></msub></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">A_1</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8333em; vertical-align: -0.15em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal">A</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.3011em;"><span style="top: -2.55em; margin-left: 0em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight">1</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> is highly positive with respect to the cathode. Electrons are accelerated from the cathode, through the holes in the grid and anode, to the focusing section of the tube.</p>
<p>(b) Focussing Section: The focussing electrodes <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msub><mi>A</mi><mn>1</mn></msub></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">A_1</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8333em; vertical-align: -0.15em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal">A</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.3011em;"><span style="top: -2.55em; margin-left: 0em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight">1</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>, <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msub><mi>A</mi><mn>2</mn></msub></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">A_2</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8333em; vertical-align: -0.15em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal">A</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.3011em;"><span style="top: -2.55em; margin-left: 0em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight">2</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> and <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msub><mi>A</mi><mn>3</mn></msub></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">A_3</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8333em; vertical-align: -0.15em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal">A</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.3011em;"><span style="top: -2.55em; margin-left: 0em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight">3</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> are called the Electron Lens. Their function is to focus the electrons to a fine point at the screen of the tube. <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msub><mi>A</mi><mn>1</mn></msub></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">A_1</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8333em; vertical-align: -0.15em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal">A</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.3011em;"><span style="top: -2.55em; margin-left: 0em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight">1</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> provides the accelerating field, to draw the electrons from the cathode, and the hole in <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msub><mi>A</mi><mn>1</mn></msub></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">A_1</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8333em; vertical-align: -0.15em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal">A</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.3011em;"><span style="top: -2.55em; margin-left: 0em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight">1</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> limits the initial cross-section of the electron beam.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-deflection-system">The Deflection System<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-deflection-system" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The electron beam can be deflected either magnetically or electrostatically. However, most of practical methods uses electrostatic deflection. An electrostatic field can be produced between two metal electrodes by applying a potential difference between them.</p>
<p><strong>Fluorescent Screen:</strong> If the electron beam leaving the electron gun were not deflected, it would produce a luminous spot at the centre of the fluorescent screen. The intensity of this spot can be controlled by adjusting the control grid bias voltage; but it also depends on the fluorescent material, called phosphor, coated on the inside surface of the tube.</p>
<p><strong>Aquadag Coating:</strong> Some measures have to be adopted to remove the electrons from the screen and return them to the cathode, or else there will be a build-up of negative charge on the screen to such an extent that it will not allow any more electrons to reach it. The method adopted, to remove the electrons from the screen is to place a conducting coating of carbon particles, called Aquadag, along the side walls of the tube, and to connect the coating to the cathode.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="6-8-4-lissajous-figures">6.8.4 Lissajous Figures<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#6-8-4-lissajous-figures" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Lissajous figures are formed when two sine waves are applied simultaneously to the vertical and horizontal deflecting plates of a CRO. The two sine waves may be obtained from two audio-oscillators. The shape of the Lissajous Pattern depends on the frequency and phase relationships of the two sine waves. Two sine waves of the same frequency and amplitude may produce a straight line, an ellipse or a circle, depending on their phase difference (Fig. 6.17).</p>
<p>In general, the shape of Lissajous figures depends on :</p>
<p>(i) amplitude
(ii) phase difference and
(iii) ratio of frequency of the two waves.</p>
<p>Introduction to Operational Amplifiers</p>
<p>Lissajous figures are used for:</p>
<p>(i) determining an unknown frequency by comparing it with a known frequency.
(ii) checking audio oscillator with a known frequency signal.
(iii) checking audio amplifiers and feedback networks for phase shift.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="measurement-of-frequency-using-lissajous-figures">Measurement of Frequency using Lissajous Figures<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#measurement-of-frequency-using-lissajous-figures" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>To measure the frequency of a sine wave voltage, it is applied to one set of deflection plates of CRO. The sinusoidal voltage obtained from a standard variable frequency oscillator is applied to other set of deflection plates. The frequency of this oscillator is varied until a suitable stationary Lissajous figure is obtained. Knowing the oscillator frequency and counting the number of times the sides of the pattern are tangent to a horizontal and a vertical line, the unknown frequency can be determined.</p>
<p>The ratio of the two frequencies is given by:</p>
<div class="math math-display"><span class="katex-display"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" display="block"><semantics><mtable width="100%"><mtr><mtd width="50%"></mtd><mtd><mrow><mfrac><msub><mi>f</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">H</mi></msub><msub><mi>f</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">v</mi></msub></mfrac><mo>=</mo><mfrac><mtext>No.&nbsp;of&nbsp;points&nbsp;of&nbsp;horizontal&nbsp;tangency</mtext><mtext>No.&nbsp;of&nbsp;points&nbsp;of&nbsp;vertical&nbsp;tangency</mtext></mfrac></mrow></mtd><mtd width="50%"></mtd><mtd><mtext>(6.23)</mtext></mtd></mtr></mtable><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\frac {f _ {\mathrm {H}}}{f _ {\mathrm {v}}} = \frac {\text {No. of points of horizontal tangency}}{\text {No. of points of vertical tangency}} \tag {6.23}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 2.2519em; <div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="soived-problems">SOIVED PROBLEMS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#soived-problems" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>An Inverting Amplifier has  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msub><mi>R</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>=</mo><mn>20</mn><mtext> </mtext><mtext>K</mtext><mi mathvariant="normal">Ω</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">R_{1} = 20 \, \text{K}\Omega</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8333em; vertical-align: -0.15em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.00773em;">R</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.3011em;"><span style="top: -2.55em; <p>Solution:</p>

<div class="math math-display"><span class="katex-display"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" display="block"><semantics><mrow><msub><mi>R</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>=</mo><msub><mi>R</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo separator="true">;</mo><mtext>I&nbsp;n&nbsp;p&nbsp;u&nbsp;t&nbsp;c&nbsp;u&nbsp;r&nbsp;r&nbsp;e&nbsp;n&nbsp;t</mtext><mo>=</mo><msub><mi>V</mi><mi>i</mi></msub><mi mathvariant="normal">/</mi><msub><mi>R</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>=</mo><msub><mi>V</mi><mi>i</mi></msub><mi mathvariant="normal">/</mi><msub><mi>R</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>=</mo><mn>1</mn><mi mathvariant="normal">/</mi><mn>20</mn><mi>K</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">Ω</mi><mo>=</mo><mn>0.05</mn><mi>m</mi><mi>A</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">.</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">R _ {1} = R _ {1};
